## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv_dt) is determined by restoring forces (functions of x), damping (functions of v), and possibly external driving (functions of t). The nonlinearity can appear in the restoring force, damping, or both.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (unforced): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (linear oscillator with periodic driving)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (position-dependent stiffness)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * tanh(c3 * v) (mixed damping model)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (time-varying stiffness)
- Combined nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x * v**2 (restoring + velocity coupling)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (sinusoidal restoring force with damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ‚Üí Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ‚Üí Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ‚Üí Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ‚Üí Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ‚Üí Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) preserve symmetry of the oscillator potential ‚Äî expect odd polynomial terms in x
- Cubic position term x**3 indicates Duffing-type nonlinearity: positive coefficient = hardening spring, negative = softening spring
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to (1 - x**2)*v indicate Van der Pol-type self-excited oscillations with amplitude-dependent damping
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) signals external periodic forcing/driving
- Products of x and v (e.g., x*v, x**2*v) indicate energy-dependent or amplitude-dependent damping mechanisms
- Position-velocity coupling x*v**2 arises from centripetal-like effects or energy-conserving nonlinear terms
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests autonomous system ‚Äî look for conservative or dissipative structures in x and v only
- Sinusoidal restoring force sin(c*x) indicates pendulum-like large-angle dynamics rather than polynomial approximation

GT: -c0*beta*v - mu*(c1 - v**c2)*v - omega0**c3*(gamma*Abs(v)**c4 + c5)*x
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to analyze whether any candidate formula can match the GT expression:

**GT:** `-0.721004421988058*v*(1 - v**2) - 1.03737009496134*v - 2.44077135428351*x*(0.0154128049692563*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 + 1)`

Let me expand this:
- `-0.721004421988058*v + 0.721004421988058*v**3 - 1.03737009496134*v - 2.44077135428351*x - 2.44077135428351*0.0154128049692563*x*|v|^(1/3)`
- `= -1.75837451694940*v + 0.721004421988058*v**3 - 2.44077135428351*x - 0.037620...x*|v|^(1/3)`

So the GT has these terms:
1. A constant times `v`
2. A constant times `v**3`
3. A constant times `x`
4. A constant times `x*|v|^(1/3)`

The key challenge is the `|v|^(1/3)` term. In candidates, this would need `v**c` with c=1/3, but `v**(1/3)` is not the same as `|v|**(1/3)` for negative v. However, many candidates have `(c + v)**(1/3)` terms, which also differ.

Let me look for candidates with the structure: `c*v + c*v**3 + c*x + c*v^(c)*x` (where the v^c could give |v|^(1/3)).

**Candidate 47:** `c0*x + c1*v + c2*v**3 + c3*v**c4*x + c5*x*(c6 + v)**(1/3)`

This has: c0*x + c1*v + c2*v**3 + c3*v^c4*x + c5*x*(c6+v)^(1/3)

If I set c6=0, this becomes: c0*x + c1*v + c2*v**3 + c3*v^c4*x + c5*x*v^(1/3)

But v^(1/3) ‚âÝ |v|^(1/3) for negative v. However, if we assume the domain is v > 0, they'd match.

Setting c3=0 (to eliminate the extra term): c0*x + c1*v + c2*v**3 + c5*x*v^(1/3)
This matches the structure! With c0 = -2.44077..., c1 = -1.75837..., c2 = 0.72100..., c5*v^(1/3) matching the |v|^(1/3) term.

**Candidate 6:** `c0*x + c1*v + c2*v**3 + c3*v*x + c4*v**c5*x + c6*x*(c7 + v)**(1/3)`

Setting c3=0 and c7=0: c0*x + c1*v + c2*v**3 + c4*v^c5*x + c6*x*v^(1/3)
Setting c4=0: c0*x + c1*v + c2*v**3 + c6*x*v^(1/3) ‚Äî same structure.

Or alternatively, setting c6=0 and c5=1/3: c0*x + c1*v + c2*v**3 + c3*v*x + c4*v^(1/3)*x ‚Äî but GT has no v*x term, so set c3=0.

**Candidate 47** works if we set c3=0, c6=0:
`c0*x + c1*v + c2*v**3 + c5*x*v^(1/3)`

With c0=-2.44077, c1=-1.75837, c2=0.72100, c5=-0.03762

This matches the GT (assuming the domain handles v^(1/3) appropriately, or that |v|^(1/3) = v^(1/3) is acceptable in the modeling context).
